r1253 | abrown | 2011-04-20 13:06:51 -0400 (Wed, 20 Apr 2011) | 17 lines

345: GPS Enhancements: Create Plot tools
Created data plot tools:
plot_est_cno.m - the estimated C/No from gps_est_cno vs time
plot_gps_cno.m - the raw GPS signal to noise ratio vs time
plot_gps_gain_2d.m -the gain from gps_gain vs azimuth and elevation angles (2D plots)
plot_gps_gain_3d.m - the gain from gps_gain or antenna gain pattern vs az and el angles (3D plots)
plot_gps_pp_azel.m - the antenna az and el angle physical parameters from gps_phys_params vs time
plot_gps_pp_gpsyaw.m - the modeled GPS yaw angle physical parameter from gps_phys_params vs time
plot_gps_pp_rrdot.m - the range and range rate physical parameters from gps_phys_params vs time
plot_gps_prange.m - the raw GPS pseudorange vs time

Updated the following files:
rinexo2gpsdata.m - updated header description line
Contents.m - ran MATLAB contents report for first cut
gps_phys_params.m - fixed typo in input description
gps_antenna_tools_demo.m - Updated demo to demonstrate the above plots
gps_antenna_tools_support.m - Bugfix to also exclude any NaNs generated by gpsmeas as this could have confused users with slightly different plots
------------------------------------------------------------------------

r1038 | smetcalfe | 2010-09-27 12:56:11 -0400 (Mon, 27 Sep 2010) | 27 lines

Issue 210:	Hermite Interpolator for when ODToolboxIntegrators time array length is less than 8. 

HermiteInterpolator was implemented and tested first as Matlab code and then in Java. The ddHermite function is the core of the Hermite Interpolator functionality. The Matlab version of ddHermite was written by Sun Hur-Diaz. The HermiteInterpolator function is a wrapper around ddHermite, used to adapt the JAT data for ddHermite. Regression/Unit Test code was written to validate the HermiteInterpolator functionality in both Matlab and Java using a simple acceleration model. These check the functionality against known good results calculated without using HermiteInterpolator. The tests use a variety of dimensions, array lengths, starting times and velocities, sampling before, at and after the first, mid and last time points in the array. The Regression/Unit Test code has also been saved in the repository. 

NB: The accuracy of the HermiteInterpolator is limited when only one time point is provided. The tests use no acceleration when there is only one time point, to validate interpolation in the only case where accuracy should be assured.

Modified    jatWorldPropagatorRKF78_regression.m
                Modified to show how to update regression data.
                Added comments to identify which interpolator gets called.

Modified    jatWorldPropagatorRKF78_regression.mat
                Modified to update regression data.

Added       ddhermite.m
                Core hermite interpolator function.

Added       HermiteInterpolator.m
                HermiteInterpolator with interface matching java code.

Added       HermiteInterpolator_regression.m
                HermiteInterpolator regression test for Matlab.

Added       HermiteInterpolator_regression_data.m
                Creates HermiteInterpolator regression test data for Matlab.

Added       HermiteInterpolator_regression_data.mat
                Regression test data for Matlab.

r794 | bbarbee | 2009-10-01 15:53:18 -0400 (Thu, 01 Oct 2009) | 21 lines

Mantis 115: Estimator Feature: UpdateVectorized

o In an effort to understand the differences between results when the
  UpdateVectorized flag is set to No and when the flag is set to Yes,
  I have modified my upvec_test.m program (in ODTBX_Examples) to make
  two estseq runs that are identical except for the UpdateVectorized
  flag. I have also added code that makes data plots of all the differences
  between all the data returned by estseq. For the data matrices that have
  too many dimensions for plotting, the min and max of the absolute value
  of their differences are printed to the screen.
  - You can simply start MATLAB and then run upvec_test to see all the data
    very quickly.
  - Setting the UpdateVectorized flag to the same value for the two runs
    yields differences that are identically zero for all values, as expected.
  - When one run has UpdateVectorized on and the other has it off, there are
    differences between quite a few of the return arguments from estseq for
    the two runs, but these differences are very, very small (tiny orders of
    magnitude). Nevertheless, there is some structure in the difference signals
    (I think).
  - More study is required to determine what sort of differences we expect to
    see. Then that expectation can be compared to the current test case.
------------------------------------------------------------------------

r764 | sun | 2009-09-15 12:23:50 -0400 (Tue, 15 Sep 2009) | 6 lines

Mantis 0000176: Estimators may not be consistently applying solve-for mapping - In the time update when j~=1 (i.e., not the first Monte Carlo case), the Phat covariance assignment does not have the right index:

                shat{j}(:,k+1) = mergesigpts(S_mnus,hbar,ns);
                Phat{j}(:,k) = scrunch(rtPss*rtPss');

Since Phat was being initialized with NaN, every other columns of Phat{j} was left as NaN.  There is no consequence on the filter computations since they are done with rtPss and not Phat.  I've changed k to k+1, and updated the self-test data as well as the regression data for estspf.

r747 | bbarbee | 2009-08-31 12:54:27 -0400 (Mon, 31 Aug 2009) | 10 lines

Mantis 166: Add gpsmeas.m Ecliptic North/South Antenna Pointing option 

o Determined that gpsmeas was not passing time correctly to comp_bs_3d. Time
  should be passed into comp_bs_3d as total seconds since start of GPS time,
  but instead it was being passed in as simulation time (starting at zero).
  The resulting error did not manifest before since we were only specifying
  Earth pointing [1, -1] previously and time does not factor into computing
  the boresite vectors in that case. The error did manifest when we began
  attempting to use the ecliptic pointing option since time is required to
  compute the boresite vectors in that case.

r742 | bbarbee | 2009-08-26 17:25:02 -0400 (Wed, 26 Aug 2009) | 10 lines

Mantis 125: New estbat option: "Ignore Process Noise"  

o Fixed a bug in estbat_no_proc_noise_test.m that was uncovered during the
  nightly regression on cypher. Essentially 4 of the variables being compared
  are expected to be identical and their differences were thus expected to be
  zero. On cypher (and Allen's computer), MATLAB was computing differences on
  the order of 10^-21 and that was tripping the check in the code. I modified
  the check in the code such that it will not expect the values to match beyond
  the machine precision (via eps), which is typically 5 orders of magnitude
  larger than 10^-21.
------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mantis 125: New estbat option: "Ignore Process Noise"  

o Added an option in odtbxOptions.m called UseProcNoise. Setting this variable
  equal to 1 causes estbat to use process noise while setting it 0 causes estbat
  to ignore process noise.
o The logic in estbat.m that utilizes this new option variable simply zeros out
  the process noise array (currently the variable name for this array is Qd in
  estbat.m).
o This new functionality was exercised and verified by modifying
  estbat_example.m such that it sets the UseProcNoise option. Currently the
  option is set to 1, which produces the exact same behavior from before this
  revision. Setting the option 
------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mantis 143: estbat: input argument documentation inconsistency

o As per CCB recommendation I have modified the 'help' section comments for
  estbat.m to direct the user to only specify the time span as tspan = [t0 t1,
  ..., tf] since using tspan = [t0 tf] (which would ostensibly allow the
  numerical integrator to select the output time step) fails. tspan = [t0 tf]
  was previously stated as an option for the user in the documentation but is
  now removed.

r636 | bbarbee | 2009-05-14 15:30:50 -0400 (Thu, 14 May 2009) | 17 lines

Mantis 131: jatRK8 needs regresstion test
Mantis 147: jatRK8 throws a java error when calculatetrueanomalystep chooses
            the stepsize for large time spans 

o Modified jatRK8.m such that user can specify the integration step-size via
  the time input argument, in the form time = (t0:dt:tf). Previously dt was
  being ignored unless the user set the step-size parameter in the options data
  structure.
o Added information in the 'help' section comments for jatRK8.m explaining to
  the user that a known error may occur when passing in time in the form
  time = [t0 tf] *and* -not- specifying a step-size in the options data structure,
  which will cause jatRK8.m to invoke calculatetrueanomalystep to compute the
  step-size. An error has been observed in this case when the time-span is
  'large', e.g., [0 86400] (whereas no error occurs for a time-span of
  [0 8640]. The number of orbit data points has been tentatively ruled-out as
  the cause of the error.
    
------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mantis 116: ConvertTime.m doesn't always handle arrays

  timescale pairs for convertTime.m.

    they were passed an array of time values:

    2:  UTC to TT, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    3:  UTC to TDB, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    4:  TT to UTC, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    5:  TT to TDB, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    6:  TDB to GPS, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    7:  TDB to UTC, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    8:  TDB to TT, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    9:  TDB to TAI, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].
    10: TAI to TDB, result size = [1 1], should be [1 3].

   - Added this test code to convertTime_test.m.

o Corrected the code in convertTime.m such that it now handles arrays of time
  values correctly for all possible to/from pairs.

r149 | kgregory | 2007-05-10 12:54:19 -0400 (Thu, 10 May 2007) | 1 line

Tagging ODTBX1.0 release for the Spiral 4 demonstration. This release contains the validated estbat and estseq estimators, the original JAT universe Adaptor and the MATLAB help system. Also included are three directories that were not part of the release. Regression contains the regression testing for the toolbox estbat and estseq functions. Metadata is an SVN repository directory. Validation is a directory that was used for validating the estbat estimator. This release was compiled by Kathryn Gregory with assistance from Russell Carpenter, Kevin Berry, Bill Bamford and Dave Gaylor. Release was created on 9 May 2007.
